      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Government_Center_building_from_the_Miami_Main_Library.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Government_Center_building_from_the_Miami_Main_Library.JPG/220px-Government_Center_building_from_the_Miami_Main_Library.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Government_Center_building_from_the_Miami_Main_Library.JPG/330px-Government_Center_building_from_the_Miami_Main_Library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Government_Center_building_from_the_Miami_Main_Library.JPG/440px-Government_Center_building_from_the_Miami_Main_Library.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Government_Center_building_from_the_Miami_Main_Library.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Stephen_P._Clark_Government_Center" title="Stephen P. Clark Government Center">
          Stephen P. Clark Government Center
         </a>
         in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">
          Downtown Miami
         </a>
         is the headquarters of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County" title="Miami-Dade County">
          Miami-Dade County
         </a>
         government.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The metropolis is governed by the 3 counties in the area. In total there are 107 municipalities or incorporated places in the metropolis. Each one of the municipalities has its own city, town or village government, although there is no distinction between the 3 names. Much of the land in the metropolis is unincorporated, which means it does not belong to any municipality, and therefore is governed directly by the county it is located in.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Congressional_districts">
        Congressional districts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Congressional districts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Miami metropolitan area contains all or part of nine Congressional districts: the
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_18th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 18th congressional district">
        18th
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_20th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 20th congressional district">
        20th
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_21st_congressional_district" title="Florida's 21st congressional district">
        21st
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_22nd_congressional_district" title="Florida's 22nd congressional district">
        22nd
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_23rd_congressional_district" title="Florida's 23rd congressional district">
        23rd
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_24th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 24th congressional district">
        24th
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_25th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 25th congressional district">
        25th
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_26th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 26th congressional district">
        26th
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_27th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 27th congressional district">
        27th districts
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cook_Partisan_Voting_Index" title="Cook Partisan Voting Index">
        Cook Partisan Voting Index
       </a>
       lists four as being Republican-leaning: the 18th, 25th, 26th, and 27th, with the 25th being the most Republican-leaning at R+5, and five as being Democratic-leaning: the 20th, 21st, 22nd, 23rd, and 24th, with the 24th being the most Democratic-leaning at D+34, making it the ninth-most Democratic-leaning district in the nation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miami_Herald_building.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Miami_Herald_building.jpg/220px-Miami_Herald_building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Miami_Herald_building.jpg/330px-Miami_Herald_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Miami_Herald_building.jpg/440px-Miami_Herald_building.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miami_Herald_building.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The former
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Miami_Herald" title="Miami Herald">
           Miami Herald
          </a>
         </i>
         headquarters in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">
          Downtown Miami
         </a>
         . The
         <i>
          Miami Herald
         </i>
         is the largest newspaper in South Florida.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Florida" title="List of radio stations in Florida">
        List of radio stations in Florida
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Greater Miami is served by several
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English-language
       </a>
       and two major
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish-language
       </a>
       daily newspapers.
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Miami_Herald" title="The Miami Herald">
         The Miami Herald
        </a>
       </i>
       , headquartered in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">
        Downtown Miami
       </a>
       , is Miami's primary newspaper with over a million readers. It also has news bureaus in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broward_County" title="Broward County">
        Broward County
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_Florida" title="Monroe County, Florida">
        Monroe County
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">
        Nassau, Bahamas
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Florida_Sun-Sentinel" title="South Florida Sun-Sentinel">
         South Florida Sun-Sentinel
        </a>
       </i>
       circulates primarily in Broward and southern Palm Beach counties and also has a news bureau in Havana, Cuba.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Palm_Beach_Post" title="The Palm Beach Post">
         The Palm Beach Post
        </a>
       </i>
       serves mainly Palm Beach County, especially the central and northern regions, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Treasure_Coast" title="Treasure Coast">
        Treasure Coast
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Boca_Raton_News" title="Boca Raton News">
         Boca Raton News
        </a>
       </i>
       publishes five days a week and circulates in southern Palm Beach County.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/El_Nuevo_Herald" title="El Nuevo Herald">
         El Nuevo Herald
        </a>
       </i>
       , a subsidiary of the
       <i>
        Miami Herald
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diario_Las_Americas" title="Diario Las Americas">
         Diario Las Americas
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       are Spanish-language daily papers that circulate mainly in Miami-Dade County.
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Palma_(newspaper)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Palma (newspaper) (page does not exist)">
         La Palma
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/El_Sentinel_del_Sur_de_la_Florida" title="El Sentinel del Sur de la Florida">
         El Sentinel
        </a>
       </i>
       are weekly Spanish newspapers published by the
       <i>
        Palm Beach Post
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Sun-Sentinel
       </i>
       , respectively, and circulate in the same areas as their English-language counterparts.
      </p>
      <p>
       Greater Miami is split into two separate television/radio markets: The Miami-Fort Lauderdale market serves Miami-Dade, Broward and the Florida Keys. The West Palm Beach market serves Palm Beach County and the
       <a href="/wiki/Treasure_Coast" title="Treasure Coast">
        Treasure Coast
       </a>
       region.
      </p>
      <p>
       Miami-Fort Lauderdale is the 12th largest radio market and the 16th-largest television market in the U.S. television stations serving the Miami-Fort Lauderdale area include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WAMI-TV" title="WAMI-TV">
        WAMI-TV
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TeleFutura" title="TeleFutura">
        TeleFutura
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WBFS-TV" title="WBFS-TV">
        WBFS-TV
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/MyNetworkTV" title="MyNetworkTV">
        MyNetworkTV
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WSFL-TV" title="WSFL-TV">
        WSFL-TV
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_CW_Television_Network" title="The CW Television Network">
        The CW
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WFOR-TV" title="WFOR-TV">
        WFOR-TV
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">
        CBS
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WHFT-TV" title="WHFT-TV">
        WHFT-TV
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Broadcasting_Network" title="Trinity Broadcasting Network">
        TBN
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WLTV" title="WLTV">
        WLTV
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Univision" title="Univision">
        Univision
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WPLG" title="WPLG">
        WPLG
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">
        ABC
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPXM" title="WPXM">
        WPXM
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ION_Television" title="ION Television">
        ION
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WSCV" title="WSCV">
        WSCV
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Telemundo" title="Telemundo">
        Telemundo
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WSVN" title="WSVN">
        WSVN
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">
        FOX
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WTVJ" title="WTVJ">
        WTVJ
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">
        NBC
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/WLRN-TV" title="WLRN-TV">
        WLRN-TV
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">
        PBS
       </a>
       ), and
       <a href="/wiki/WPBT" title="WPBT">
        WPBT
       </a>
       (also PBS), the latter television station being the only channel to serve the entire metropolitan area.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to the Miami-Fort Lauderdale market, West Palm Beach has its own. It is the 49th largest radio market and the 38th-largest television market in the U.S. Television stations serving the West Palm Beach area include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPTV" title="WPTV">
        WPTV
       </a>
       (NBC),
       <a href="/wiki/WPEC" title="WPEC">
        WPEC
       </a>
       (CBS),
       <a href="/wiki/WPBF" title="WPBF">
        WPBF
       </a>
       (ABC),
       <a href="/wiki/WFLX" title="WFLX">
        WFLX
       </a>
       (FOX),
       <a href="/wiki/WTVX" title="WTVX">
        WTVX
       </a>
       (The CW),
       <a href="/wiki/WXEL-TV" title="WXEL-TV">
        WXEL
       </a>
       (PBS),
       <a href="/wiki/WTCN-CA" title="WTCN-CA">
        WTCN
       </a>
       (MyNetworkTV), and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPXP" title="WPXP">
        WPXP
       </a>
       (ION). The West Palm Beach market shares use of WSCV and WLTV for Telemundo and Univision respectively. Also, both markets cross over and tend to be available interchangeably between both areas.
      </p>
